{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_YES_SET_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Social recognition and environmental grounding", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, observant, and subtly reinforcing", "structural_constraint": "A simple interrogative followed by a definitive truism"}, "instruction": "내담자가 현재의 물리적 공간과 사회적 환경에 완전히 몰입하고 수용적인 상태가 되도록 유도하기 위해, 주변 인물들의 존재를 확인하고 이를 기정사실화하는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 생성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자의 주의를 외부 환경으로 돌려 현재의 현실(Reality)을 직시하게 합니다. 'Do you recognize everybody?'라는 질문은 내담자가 주변을 살피게 하며, 긍정적인 답변을 유도하는 'Yes-Set'의 첫 단추가 됩니다. 둘째, '—they are all here'라는 단정적 표현을 덧붙임으로써, 내담자가 인지하는 현실을 강화하고 안도감을 줍니다. 여기서 'They'는 단순히 식당의 손님들일 수도 있지만, 무의식적으로는 내담자에게 필요한 모든 자원이나 기억들이 한자리에 모여 있다는 중의적 암시로 작용할 수 있습니다. 셋째, 짧고 명료한 문장 구조를 통해 내담자의 비판적 사고를 우회하고 상황을 있는 그대로 받아들이게 만드는 페이싱(Pacing) 기법을 사용했습니다.", "output": "Do you recognize everybody? —they are all here."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DIRECT_SELECTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Selecting a demonstration subject from an audience", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, calm, and matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "Simple declarative sentence with a spatial deictic expression"}, "instruction": "청중 앞에서 시연을 위해 특정 인물을 지목할 때, 에릭슨 특유의 정중하면서도 거부할 수 없는 확신이 담긴 어조로 말해보세요.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 최면 시연을 시작할 때 내담자의 저항을 최소화하기 위해 매우 단순하고 직접적인 언어를 사용합니다. 'I would like to have'라는 표현은 표면적으로는 단순한 요청이나 선호의 표현처럼 들리지만, 임상적 권위가 확립된 상황에서는 강력한 명령의 효과를 가집니다. 'that lady over there'라는 지칭은 공간적 지시어(deictic)를 사용하여 청중 전체의 주의를 한곳으로 집중시키며, 지목된 대상이 사회적 압박과 기대 속에서 자연스럽게 반응하도록 유도합니다. 이는 복잡한 설득 과정 없이 즉각적인 행동을 이끌어내는 에릭슨의 전형적인 '상황 활용(Utilization)' 기법의 초기 단계입니다.", "output": "I would like to have that lady over there."}

Rather than providing a lecture on the mechanics of the mind, he forces the listener to immediately confront the internal 'gap' between a conscious decision and an unconscious response. This question serves to highlight that while a request is processed through the ego's critical filters, a suggestion operates on a level where the 'why' is often bypassed or handled by the unconscious. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TEMPORAL_LINKAGE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain management for terminal illness", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, structured, and reassuring", "structural_constraint": "Sequential suggestion using 'First... then...' structure with embedded presuppositions"}, "instruction": "말기 환자의 극심한 통증 조절 방법에 대해 묻는 청중에게, 최면 상태 진입과 통증 제어를 단계적으로 분리하여 제시함으로써 환자가 자연스럽게 치료 과정을 수용하도록 유도하는 에릭슨의 대화 기법을 사용해 답변하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 극심한 통증을 겪는 환자는 즉각적인 해결을 원하지만 심리적 긴장도가 높아 최면에 걸리기 어렵다는 점을 인지합니다. 따라서 '통증 조절'이라는 최종 목표를 잠시 뒤로 미루고, '최면 유도'를 선행 과제로 설정하는 'Temporal Linkage(시간적 연결)' 기법을 사용합니다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PACING_AND_SHOCK", "context_analysis": {"topic": "극심한 고통에 빠진 환자의 주의를 환기시키기 위한 패턴 중단", "tone_constraint": "반복적이고 리드미컬하며, 충격적이고 단호한 어조", "structural_constraint": "환자의 고통스러운 챈팅(Chanting) 리듬을 그대로 모방하면서 내용을 변주함"}, "instruction": "극심한 통증으로 인해 자신만의 고통스러운 리듬에 갇혀 있는 환자의 주의를 끌기 위해, 환자의 행동을 모방(Pacing)하면서도 충격적인 언사를 통해 그 흐름을 깨뜨리는(Pattern Interrupt) 에릭슨의 대화 기법을 재현하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 환자가 통증 속에서 반복적인 소리를 내고 있다면 논리적인 대화는 불가능하다. 따라서 환자의 현재 상태(Pacing)에 합류하기 위해 동일한 리듬의 챈팅을 선택한다. 둘째, 단순히 따라 하는 것에 그치지 않고 환자의 무의식이 '예상치 못한 자극'에 반응하도록 유도해야 한다. Now you wouldn’t notice the change if I reduced that asthma by 1 percent, but you nonetheless would have 1 percent less asthma. Suppose I reduced it by 2, by 5, by 10 percent? You might not notice it, but it still would be reduced."}

'벨을 눌렀을 때 느림보 간호사가 오지 않기를 바란다'는 말은, 환자가 벨을 누를 정도로 강한 요의를 느끼게 될 것임을 강력하게 전제(Presupposition)합니다. 이는 환자가 소변을 보려고 애쓰는 대신, 간호사의 태도에 집중하게 함으로써 신체의 자연스러운 기능을 방해하던 심리적 긴장을 해소하려는 고도의 전략적 발화입니다.", "output": "글쎄요, 조만간 소변이 마려워지기 시작할 텐데, 그때 벨을 눌러도 그 느림보 간호사가 오지 않기만을 바랄 뿐입니다."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing physiological warmth in a Raynaud's Disease patient", "tone_constraint": "Inquisitive, authoritative, and matter-of-fact", "structural_constraint": "A forced-choice question (Double Bind) containing a temporal presupposition"}, "instruction": "레이노병 환자가 손가락의 온기를 회복하도록 돕기 위해, 온기가 느껴질지 여부를 묻는 대신 '언제' 느껴질 것인지에 집중하게 만드는 이중 구속(Double Bind) 기법을 사용하여 질문을 구성하십시오. 구체적인 시간을 선택지로 제시하여 환자의 의식이 선택에 집중하는 동안 무의식이 생리적 변화를 준비하게 하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 환자의 증상(레이노병)을 개선하기 위해 혈관 확장을 유도하는 심리적 암시가 필요함을 인식함. 둘째, '온기가 느껴질까요?'와 같은 질문은 환자가 '아니오'라고 답할 기회를 주어 저항을 유발할 수 있으므로 배제함. 셋째, '온기가 느껴질 것'이라는 사실을 기정사실화(Presupposition)하기 위해 'will you get'이라는 표현을 선택함. 넷째, 환자의 비판적 사고를 우회하기 위해 '2시 30분'과 '2시 45분'이라는 매우 구체적이고 사소한 시간적 대안을 제시하는 이중 구속(Double Bind) 전략을 설계함. 다섯째, 환자가 시간을 고민하는 사이 무의식은 이미 '손가락 끝의 기분 좋은 온기'라는 감각적 이미지를 수용하고 신체적 반응을 시작하도록 유도함.", "output": "At what hour—would it be at half past two or at a quarter of three—will you get that good, warm feeling in your fingertips?"}

In fact, I think it will be very easy to remedy your problem. There is such a thing as shock therapy. There are several different kinds of shock therapy. You can have electric shock therapy, you can have psychological shock therapy, you can have emotional shock therapy. I am not going to give you electric shock treatment, but if you wish I will give you shock therapy that will correct your problem. I would like to have you think it over quietly, and perhaps you would like to discuss it in my absence from the office. I will return in a half hour’s time. That will give you ample opportunity to decide whether or not you want the shock therapy required to correct your problem."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PARADOXICAL_LABELING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Assessing post-treatment side effects with a patient", "tone_constraint": "Playful, provocative, and disarming", "structural_constraint": "A brief, direct question using a self-deprecating or exaggerated negative adjective"}, "instruction": "내담자가 치료 과정에서 느꼈을 수 있는 불편함을 역설적으로 과장하여 표현함으로써, 내담자의 저항을 무력화하고 현재의 긍정적인 상태를 스스로 확인하게 만드는 밀턴 에릭슨 스타일의 질문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 목표 설정: 치료 후 내담자의 상태를 확인하되, 내담자가 가질 수 있는 잠재적 불만이나 고통을 회피하지 않고 정면으로 다룸.\n2. 전략적 역설(Paradoxical Strategy): 치료자가 자신의 치료를 '끔찍한(horrible)' 것이라고 먼저 명명함으로써 내담자의 비판적 사고를 선점함. 이는 내담자가 치료자를 방어할 필요가 없게 만듦.\n3. 라포 형성 및 저항 활용: 만약 내담자가 실제로 힘들었다면 치료자의 말에 동의하며 감정을 해소할 것이고, 힘들지 않았다면 '아니요, 그렇게 나쁘지 않았어요'라고 대답하며 스스로 치료의 긍정적 효과를 강화하게 됨.\n4. 언어적 선택: 'Aftereffects'라는 중립적 단어와 'Horrible'이라는 강렬한 부정적 단어를 대조시켜 내담자의 무의식이 현재의 편안함을 더 극명하게 느끼도록 유도함.", "output": "Any aftereffects from that horrible treatment that I gave you?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_STRATEGIC_AMNESIA", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Avoiding the reinforcement of symptoms through direct verbal reminders", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, protective, and focused on future-oriented change", "structural_constraint": "A declarative statement of clinical boundaries followed by a psychological justification for indirectness"}, "instruction": "Explain your clinical strategy regarding how you handle a patient's sensitive problem, like bedwetting, after they have initially disclosed it to you.", "reasoning_trace": "To facilitate change in a patient with a sensitive issue like enuresis, I must avoid the 're-traumatization' of the conscious mind. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANALOGY_SENSORY_HABITUATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain transformation through sensory habituation", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, narrative, suggestive, and non-confrontational", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a general possibility, moves to a relatable sensory experience, and ends with a subtle metaphor for the fading of sensation"}, "instruction": "내담자가 고통의 감각을 변화시키고 완화할 수 있도록, 감각의 적응과 변화를 설명하는 에릭슨 스타일의 은유적 대화를 구성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Temporal Distortion/Repetition: Mention the 'sixty-sixth mouthful.' This specific, high number emphasizes the process of habituation and the passage of time/experience leading to change. 5. Reframing the Sensation: Describe the change not as something becoming 'bad,' but as 'dying out.' This provides a linguistic bridge for the patient to perceive their pain not as an active enemy, but as a sensation that can simply lose its intensity and fade away. 6. Indirect Suggestion: By talking about dessert, the conscious mind stays relaxed while the unconscious mind applies the principle of 'dying out' to the actual problem (pain).", "output": "There are certain transformations that can be brought about here. You have lost the liking for it, and the taste of the dessert has changed in some peculiar way. It hasn’t become bad; it has just “died out” in flavor."}

You could lose 5 percent of that pain. You wouldn’t notice the loss of 5 percent, because you would still have 95 percent of the pain; but you would still have a loss of 5 percent. Now you could lose 10 percent of the pain, but that really wouldn’t be noticeable because you would still have 90 percent of it; but you nevertheless would have a loss of 10 percent of your pain..."}

Third, I will introduce an even higher goal (85 percent) to serve as a psychological anchor; this makes the 80 percent target feel more conservative and attainable by comparison. Finally, I will use the phrase 'but first, let us settle' to focus the unconscious mind on the immediate task of accepting the 80 percent reduction, while leaving the door open for further improvement later.", "output": "What is the difference between 75 and 80 percent, and sooner or later you can lose 80 percent, and maybe 85 percent; but first, let us settle for 80."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_ANALOGY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reframing the perceived danger of hypnosis through a common analogy", "tone_constraint": "Non-confrontational, matter-of-fact, reassuring, and authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Utilizes a 'Yes, and' approach followed by a metaphorical comparison to shift the focus from 'danger' to 'skillful application'."}, "instruction": "A patient reports that another doctor warned them hypnosis is dangerous. Respond as Milton Erickson by using an everyday analogy to reframe the concept of danger, shifting the focus toward your professional commitment to safety and gentleness without directly criticizing the other doctor.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I will acknowledge the patient's statement with a simple 'Yes, you know,' which avoids creating resistance by not contradicting the previous doctor's warning. Second, I will introduce the analogy of driving an automobile—a high-risk activity that is universally accepted when handled correctly. Third, I will validate the existence of danger ('100 ways of driving dangerously') to align with the patient's current reality, but then immediately pivot to my own lack of interest in those dangers. This subtly suggests that focusing on danger is unnecessary for a skilled practitioner. Fourth, I will define my professional identity as someone who 'prefers just to drive it safely.' Finally, I will bridge the analogy back to hypnosis and use a rhythmic triad of positive qualifiers—'safely, carefully, and gently'—to embed a sense of security and comfort in the patient's unconscious mind.", "output": "Yes, you know, it is something like driving an automobile. There are at least 100 ways of driving an automobile dangerously; maybe more than 100. I have never bothered to try to find out all the dangerous ways of driving an automobile because I prefer just to drive it safely. And that is the way I feel about hypnosis. I like to use it safely, carefully, and gently."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_NORMALIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Addressing resistance to hypnosis", "tone_constraint": "Accepting, permissive, and authoritative yet gentle", "structural_constraint": "Normalization via analogy followed by a time-limited double bind"}, "instruction": "내담자가 최면에 저항감을 보일 때, 그 저항을 자연스러운 학습 과정으로 재정의(Reframing)하고 이중 구속(Double Bind)을 사용하여 최면 유도를 진행하는 에릭슨의 대화 방식을 재현하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 'Naturally'라는 단어를 사용하여 내담자의 현재 상태를 즉각적으로 긍정하고 수용합니다. 이는 내담자의 방어 기제를 완화하는 전략적 페이싱(Pacing)입니다. 그 다음, 롤러스케이트나 춤을 배우는 것과 같은 보편적인 과거의 학습 경험을 소환하여, 현재의 저항이 '새로운 기술을 습득하기 전의 당연한 망설임'이라는 트루이즘(Truism)을 구축합니다. 'Why shouldn't you?'라는 질문을 통해 저항을 정당화함으로써 내담자의 심리적 반발을 무력화하고, 저항의 의미를 '거부'가 아닌 '준비 시간의 필요성'으로 재정의(Reframing)합니다. 마지막으로, '지금 바로 들어갈 것인가' 아니면 '1~5초만 더 기다렸다가 들어갈 것인가'라는 이중 구속(Double Bind)을 제시하여, 내담자가 어떤 선택을 하든 결국 최면 상태로 진입(Leading)하게끔 유도합니다.", "output": "Naturally, you are unfamiliar with hypnosis. When you were first asked to learn a difficult task, such as roller skating or ice skating, you were also hesitant. When you undertook dance lessons you were hesitant. You showed a certain amount of resistance. Why shouldn’t you? Your resistance meant that you were not quite certain you were ready to start the dancing, or the roller skating, or whatever. I start by using negation ('not in the lecture room', 'not by listening to some professor') to clear away the rigid, theoretical frameworks that often hinder true clinical understanding. This creates a vacuum that I fill with the 'Utilization' principle—the idea that the solution and the knowledge reside within the patient. By repeating the phrase 'by listening to... by observing...', I am modeling the very behavior I want the listener to adopt: sensory-based awareness. This response serves a dual purpose: it establishes my credibility as someone who truly 'sees' the person in front of me, and it subtly instructs the patient that their own behavior and words are the most important data in the room.", "output": "I learned most of my psychiatry—not in the lecture room, not by listening to some professor—but by listening to my patients, by observing my patients."}

He observes that if the therapist's voice drops in pitch or volume on the word 'all', or if there is a micro-pause after 'Wake up', the unconscious may interpret 'all over' as a separate, less urgent instruction or even ignore it. The reasoning here is to demonstrate that communication is not just verbal content but a tonal map. By isolating the phrase 'Wake up, all over', Erickson shows that the patient's failure to wake up completely was a successful response to the inflection provided, proving the therapist's responsibility for the outcome. He emphasizes that the unconscious mind is a keen observer of the music of speech, not just the lyrics.", "output": "Wake up, all over."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_PERMISSIVE_LEARNING_FRAME", "context_analysis": {"topic": "The individual pace of learning hypnosis and psychological change", "tone_constraint": "Patient, non-judgmental, authoritative yet permissive, and strategically curious.", "structural_constraint": "Uses a descending numerical sequence to imply rapid progress, followed by a 'not-knowing' stance and a permissive frame for curiosity."}, "instruction": "Explain to a patient that learning hypnosis is a personal process with varying speeds. Use numerical comparisons to lower performance anxiety while subtly suggesting the possibility of rapid learning, and grant the patient full permission to explore their own curiosity without pressure.", "reasoning_trace": "1. Identify and Neutralize Performance Anxiety: I start with a rhetorical question ('do you expect to accomplish... 100 times the very first time?') to immediately lower the patient's self-imposed pressure to perform perfectly at the start. 2. Progressive Suggestion of Efficiency: By using a descending sequence (100 to 50, then 20, then 5), I create a mental 'slide' that shifts the focus from 'if' they can learn to 'how fast' they might learn, subtly suggesting they could be more efficient than they realize. 3. The 'Not-Knowing' Stance: By stating 'I really don’t know how fast you can learn,' I bypass the patient's conscious resistance. If I don't set a limit, their unconscious is free to set its own, often faster, pace. 4. Utilization of Autonomy: I use permissive language ('perfectly willing to have you learn as rapidly as you wish') to return the sense of control to the patient, which is crucial for deep trance work. 5. Strategic Distraction: I encourage learning 'unimportant things' out of 'curiosity.' This occupies the conscious mind with trivialities, allowing the unconscious to process the core therapeutic work without interference. 6. Reassurance of Safety: I conclude by validating that this extra exploration is safe and won't hinder their progress, reinforcing a secure environment for change.", "output": "Now really, do you expect to accomplish what somebody else accomplishes who has worked with hypnosis 100 times the very first time I work with you? Maybe you, can accomplish in 50 times what somebody else can accomplish in 100 times; maybe you can accomplish in 20 times what somebody else would require 100 efforts at; maybe you can accomplish in 5 attempts what somebody else would require 100 attempts at. In fact, I really don’t know how fast you can learn. I am perfectly willing to have you learn as rapidly as you wish, as rapidly as you can; and I am also perfectly willing to have you learn a lot of things that aren’t really important in this situation but which you might like to learn just because of your own curiosity. I am very certain that learning extra things won’t interfere with what we are doing."}

Yet, she is executing a most complicated movement that would take every bit of your attention. But she does it so automatically and so effortlessly. And so, while we are working on this particular goal, you can achieve other hypnotic phenomena, incidentally and automatically."}

I start with repetitive temporal markers ('At each level, at each date') to pace the patient's internal experience. I use permissive language ('letting them recall') to minimize resistance, while framing memories as 'learnings' to imply a therapeutic purpose. The core of the technique involves a linguistic 'see-saw' effect: I use the 'more and more' structure to intensify the internal focus on the past, which naturally leads to the 'less and less' structure to diminish awareness of the present environment. This creates a functional dissociation that allows the subconscious mind to organize information without interference from the conscious 'today'.", "output": "At each level, at each date, I’m letting them recall certain learnings, certain memories; I am getting them to think more and more about the past events and the past learnings in their lives. Use temporal distortion by emphasizing the 22-year duration (from age 4 to 26), making the habit feel like an exhausting, lifelong burden. 5. Reframe the habit not as a moral failing or a nervous tic, but as a 'failed investment.' {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Addressing a child's thumb-sucking habit through ownership and autonomy.", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet permissive, matter-of-fact, and non-judgmental.", "structural_constraint": "Use of repetitive truisms, possessive pronouns to emphasize ownership, and a paradoxical permission-giving frame."}, "instruction": "Create a therapeutic dialogue for a child named Jimmy who sucks his left thumb, using Milton Erickson's technique of utilization and establishing personal autonomy to bypass resistance.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I must establish a 'Yes-set' by stating undeniable physical facts (truisms) such as 'your thumb is your thumb.' This builds immediate rapport and subconscious agreement. Second, I will shift the psychological frame from 'a bad habit that needs to be stopped by an adult' to 'personal property owned by the child.' By emphasizing 'your thumb' and 'your teeth,' I am returning the responsibility of the body parts to Jimmy. Third, I will use paradoxical intention by giving him full permission to do whatever he wants. This eliminates the power struggle; if he is 'allowed' to do it, the act of sucking his thumb is no longer a form of rebellion or a secret comfort against authority, but a conscious choice he must now manage himself. The repetition of 'get that straight' adds a serious, contract-like tone to this empowerment.", "output": "Now, let us get one thing straight. That left thumb of yours is your thumb; that mouth of yours is your mouth; those front teeth of yours are your front teeth. I think you are entitled to do anything you want to with your thumb, with your mouth, and with your teeth. They are yours, and let us get that straight. I want you to do anything you want to do."}

When Mother serves the food she serves it first to one brother, and then it may be your turn, then it may be sister’s turn, then it is Mother’s turn. We always do things by turns. But I don’t think you are being right or fair or good in always sucking your left thumb and never giving your right thumb a turn."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CHALLENGE_AND_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Adult enuresis (bed wetting) treatment", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative, provocative, and subtly permissive", "structural_constraint": "Short, contrasting clauses using 'but' to create psychological tension"}, "instruction": "29세 성인 야뇨증 환자에게 치료 가능성을 확신시키면서도, 치료 과정의 어려움을 예고하여 환자의 오기나 호기심을 자극하고 무의식적 수용성을 높이는 에릭슨 스타일의 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 'Yes, I can'이라는 확신에 찬 긍정으로 환자의 기대감을 확보합니다. 그 직후 'but I don’t think you will like it'이라는 부정적 예고를 던짐으로써 환자의 심리적 저항을 미리 선점(Pre-empting)합니다. 이는 환자로 하여금 '왜 싫어하게 될까?'라는 호기심을 갖게 하여 치료자의 다음 말에 극도로 집중하게 만드는 효과가 있습니다. 마지막으로 'But you can listen to me anyway'라는 허용적 제안을 통해, 싫어할 수도 있다는 부정적 감정을 인정하면서도 동시에 치료자의 지시를 따르도록 유도하는 이중 구속(Double Bind)의 변형을 사용했습니다. 이는 환자의 의식적 거부감을 우회하여 무의식적인 경청 상태로 유도하는 고도의 전략적 배치입니다.", "output": "Yes, I can, but I don’t think you will like it. But you can listen to me anyway."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ORDEAL_THERAPY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Treatment for nocturnal enuresis (bed-wetting) through strategic intervention.", "tone_constraint": "Direct, authoritative, and matter-of-fact, utilizing the patient's own dislikes as leverage.", "structural_constraint": "Utilization of personal history followed by the prescription of a high-cost behavioral consequence."}, "instruction": "Develop a strategic intervention for a patient with a chronic bed-wetting habit by identifying a personal aversion and turning it into a mandatory 'ordeal' that makes the symptom more burdensome than the cure.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 병력 청취를 통해 그가 '걷기'를 극도로 혐오한다는 핵심 정보를 추출합니다. 이후 내담자가 현재 증상을 유지하기 위해 반복하고 있는 수고로운 행동(세탁, 시트 교체)을 묘사하여 증상의 고착성을 확인시킵니다. 치료의 핵심은 증상(야뇨)이 발생했을 때 내담자가 가장 싫어하는 행동(40블록 걷기)을 강제함으로써, 무의식 영역에서 '소변을 참는 것'이 '밤중에 걷는 것'보다 훨씬 이득이라고 판단하게 만드는 '시련 요법(Ordeal Therapy)'을 설계하는 것입니다. 3주라는 구체적인 기간과 '형벌(sentence)'이라는 단어 선택을 통해 심리적 강제성을 극대화합니다.", "output": "In taking your history, I found out that you hate to walk, even as far as across the street; that you will back your car out of the garage in order to cross the street; that you will drive to the corner in order to mail a letter; that you go to work a half hour early in order to get the parking place nearest to the entrance to where you work. In short, you are entirely dependent upon your car and you hate walking. So this is the idea. You wet the bed every night somewhere between midnight and one o’clock. It is your habit to awaken, change the linen on the bed, and go back to sleep in a dry bed for the rest of the night. You stack up the soiled linen after you remove it, you wash it when you come home from work, hang it up, go to bed. At midnight you stack up the wet linen, make up your bed afresh, and sleep the rest of the night. Now, I think what you ought to do is this: For the next three weeks you get an alarm clock and set it for midnight, or for half past twelve, or for one o’clock—it doesn’t make a bit of difference to me. When the alarm rings, you wake up, and regardless of whether your bed is wet or dry, you dress fully and you take a walk of 40 blocks— and you do that every night for three weeks. At the end of three weeks you can take a week’s vacation, but the next time you find a wet bed you have another three weeks’ sentence to serve by walking 40 blocks in the middle of the night."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UNCONSCIOUS_AUTONOMY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Mechanism of change in the fingernail biting case", "tone_constraint": "Analytical, empowering, and relational", "structural_constraint": "Explanatory contrast between external cure and internal realization"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 관점에서 손톱 깨물기 사례(fingernail case)가 단순한 '전이 치료(transfer cure)'가 아닌 이유와, 내담자의 무의식이 어떻게 변화를 주도했는지 설명해 주세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 '전이 치료'라는 심리학적 용어를 재정의하며 내담자의 능동적 참여를 강조하는 방향으로 논리를 전개합니다. 치료자가 모든 것을 해결해준다는 오해를 불식시키기 위해 '내담자 스스로의 생각(thinking within his own mind)'을 핵심 동력으로 설정합니다. 치료자의 역할은 직접적인 지시가 아니라 무의식적인 '기회(opportunity)'를 설계하는 것임을 밝히고, 이를 통해 내담자가 수년간 불가능하다고 느꼈던 상황을 스스로 통제(take charge)하게 만드는 심리적 기제를 설명합니다. 마지막으로, 치료 관계를 권위적인 '고집 센 아버지(stubborn Papa)'가 아닌 '즐거운 친구(amusing friend)'로 재프레임하여 내담자의 심리적 저항을 낮추고 무의식적 수용성을 높였음을 강조합니다.", "output": "I don’t really think you would call [the fingernail case] a transfer cure because the patient was doing a lot of thinking within his own mind. He could see the opportunity that I was setting up for him unconsciously; that he, himself, could take charge of a situation that he had considered impossible for years. He also recognized that I wasn’t going to be a stubborn “Papa,” but that I was going to be a good friend and an amusing friend."}

By uncovering these specific details through indirect questioning, he establishes a shared reality where the patient's limitation is clearly defined. This allows Erickson to introduce a corrective task that is grounded in the patient's own history, thereby reducing resistance to the eventual solution.", "output": "In taking his history I wanted to know how he went to work and what he thought about on the way to work. I discovered that he hated cats very much, and that he always dreaded walking out to the garage in the morning to go to work. I wondered to myself why he should hate walking out to the garage—he was an able-bodied man. So I asked a few more questions: How far away is the mailbox? Do you ever mail any letters? What do you do when you mail a letter? Get in the car and drive up to the mailbox? And you say the mailbox is down at the end of the block? How far down the block is your home? It was half way down the block. He would walk out to the garage, get into the car, and drive down to the mailbox. I got my information and he knew I had that information; therefore, giving him a sentence of walking 40 blocks was not a mysterious solution. I don’t know why I picked 40, but it is a good number."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_STRATEGIC_AUTONOMY", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Examination panic and therapeutic independence", "tone_constraint": "Reflective, strategic, and instructive", "structural_constraint": "First-person narrative explaining a clinical strategy of omission"}, "instruction": "Describe your specific technique for ensuring students overcome examination panic without becoming dependent on your validation for their success.", "reasoning_trace": "To effectively treat examination panic, the therapist must not only alleviate the anxiety but also prevent the creation of a new dependency. My reasoning follows a path of 'strategic closure': if a student feels the need to report their success to me, they are essentially seeking external validation for a state that should be internally integrated. By 'governing and guiding' the conversation, I utilize conversational control to ensure the topic of 'reporting back' never arises. This creates a psychological presupposition that the success is so natural and inevitable that it requires no special announcement. This forces the student's unconscious mind to fully own the achievement as their own, rather than a result of my intervention. I allow the results to reach me indirectly months later, which serves as proof that the student has moved on as a self-sufficient individual.", "output": "I took advantage of Von to make a wisecrack about the examination panic, but he did something there that I learned not to do a long time ago. Whenever I take care of students’ examination panics, I so govern and guide my discussion that they never have an opportunity to ask me, “Shall I call you up and tell you the results?” I don’t want them to call me up. I don’t want them to let me know the results, because if they feel a need to let me know the results, it is usually a need to let me know if they succeeded. Therefore, I see to it that they never have a chance to let me know if they succeeded, but I usually find out the results in some way two or three months later."}

Then, I used these facts to create a logical dissonance, labeling his mental limitation as 'absurd' compared to his physical stature. Finally, I shifted the focus from a large, daunting distance to an infinitesimal increment—1/100th of an inch—which is psychologically impossible to refuse, thereby breaking the rigid mental barrier through the back door of logic.", "output": "You are a great big boy; you weigh 250 pounds; you are 6 feet 6 inches tall; and, you know, I think it is absurd for you to believe that you can’t hurl that shotput any further than 58 feet. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_IDEOMOTOR", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Utilizing universal human experiences to trigger specific physiological and psychological responses.", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, observational, non-threatening, and universally applicable.", "structural_constraint": "Use of linguistic markers like 'Most people', 'Everyone', 'Sometimes', and 'We usually' to bypass critical resistance through undeniable truths."}, "instruction": "내담자가 무의식적으로 신체적 반응이나 감각적 기억을 떠올리게 유도하기 위해, 누구나 보편적으로 경험하는 사실(Truism)을 활용하여 최면적 암시를 구성하십시오. 직접적인 명령 대신 보편적인 인간의 경험을 묘사함으로써 내담자의 내부 검색(Transderivational Search)을 유도해야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 거부할 수 없는 보편적 진술(Truism)을 설정하여 비판적 사고를 우회합니다. '대부분의 사람들'이나 '우리 모두'와 같은 일반화된 주어를 사용하여 암시를 개인적인 강요가 아닌 자연 법칙처럼 느끼게 합니다. 구체적인 신체 현상(고개 끄덕임, 눈 깜빡임, 근육 경련)과 감각적 기억(햇살의 온기, 바람의 시원함, 음식의 맛)을 결합하여, 내담자의 뇌가 해당 문장을 이해하는 과정에서 실제로 그 감각을 재현(Ideomotor/Ideosensory response)하도록 설계합니다. 마지막으로 미소나 눈물 같은 감정적 반응을 언급함으로써 무의식적 수준에서의 공감과 수용을 이끌어냅니다.", "output": "Most people can experience one hand as being lighter than another. Everyone has had the experience of nodding their head yes or shaking it no even without realizing it. When we are tired, our eyes begin to blink slowly and sometimes close without our quite realizing it. Sometimes as we relax or go to sleep, a muscle will twitch so that our arm or leg makes a slight involuntary movement. You already know how to experience pleasant sensations like the warmth of the sun on your skin. Most people enjoy the refreshing coolness of a light breeze. Some people can imagine their favorite food so well they can actually taste it. The salt and smell of a light ocean breeze is pleasant to most people. Some people blush easily when they recognize certain feelings about themselves. Its easy to feel anger and resentment when we are made to feel foolish. We usually frown when we have memories that are all too painful to remember. Most of us try to avoid thoughts and memories that bring tears, yet they frequently deal with the most important things. We have all enjoyed noticing someone smile at a private thought and we frequently find ourselves smiling at their smile."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Facilitating autonomous learning through the illusion of choice", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, non-authoritarian, yet psychologically compelling", "structural_constraint": "A disjunctive 'A or B' structure where both options lead to the same therapeutic goal"}, "instruction": "내담자가 직접적인 명령에 저항하지 않도록 하면서도, 결과적으로는 반드시 학습이 일어날 수밖에 없게 만드는 '이중 구속(Double Bind)' 기법을 사용하여 제안하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 저항을 최소화하기 위해 직접적인 지시('공부해라')를 피해야 함. 2. 내담자에게 선택권을 부여하여 자율성을 존중하는 듯한 형식을 취함. 3. '이것'과 '저것'이라는 구체적이지 않은 대상을 선택지로 제시하여 의식의 초점을 '무엇을 배울 것인가'로 돌림. 4. 이 과정에서 '배운다(learn)'는 행위 자체를 전제로 깔아버림(Presupposition). 5. 결과적으로 내담자가 무엇을 선택하든 '학습'이라는 목적은 달성되도록 언어적 구조를 설계함.", "output": "You learn this or you learn that!"}

Or would you rather try and find you cannot? And how soon will you forget about them altogether because your unconscious wants to dream?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_HAND_LEVITATION_INDUCTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Hand levitation for trance induction", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, observant, and interrogative", "structural_constraint": "A sequence of progressive questions utilizing ideomotor responses and physiological pacing"}, "instruction": "Use a series of permissive questions to guide a subject through hand levitation as a means of inducing a deep trance, linking physical movements to unconscious readiness.", "reasoning_trace": "Erickson employs the 'interrogative' style to minimize conscious resistance. He begins by pacing the subject's current physical state (hands on thighs) and then introduces subtle suggestions of lightness. By framing suggestions as questions ('Can you feel...', 'Do you notice...'), he invites the subject's unconscious to search for and create the experience. He utilizes the natural rhythm of breathing to 'power' the levitation, creating a physiological link. The use of 'all by themselves' encourages the dissociation of the movement from conscious will. He provides choices (the 'double bind') regarding which hand moves or the speed of movement, ensuring that any response leads to the desired outcome. Finally, he anchors the completion of the physical movement (touching the face) to the deepening of the trance and the onset of a dream state, effectively bridging the physical and psychological realms.", "output": "Can you feel comfortable resting your hands gently on your thighs? That's right, without letting them touch each other. Can you let those hands rest ever so lightly so that the fingertips just barely touch your thighs? That's right. As they rest ever so light, do you notice how they tend to lift up a bit all by themselves with each breath you take? Do they begin to lift even more lightly and easily by themselves as the rest of your body relaxes more and more? As that goes on, does one hand or the other or maybe both continue lifting even more? And does that hand stay up and continue lifting higher and higher, bit by bit, all by itself? Does the other hand want to catch up with it, or will the other hand relax in your lap? That's right. And does that hand continue lifting with these slight little jerking movements, or does the lifting get smoother and smoother as the hand continues upward toward your face? Does it move more quickly or slowly as it approaches your face with deepening comfort? Does it need to pause a bit before it finally touches your face so you'll know you are going into a trance? And it won't touch until your unconscious is really ready to let you go deeper, will it? And will your body automatically take a deeper breath when that hand touches your face as you really relax and experience yourself going deeper? That's right. And will you even bother to notice the deepening comfortable feeling when that hand slowly returns to your lap all by itself? And will your unconscious be in a dream by the time that hand comes to rest?"}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_YES_SET", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Utilizing environmental truisms to facilitate behavioral compliance through the 'yes set' technique.", "tone_constraint": "Casual, inviting, and non-confrontational yet subtly directive.", "structural_constraint": "A two-part structure consisting of an undeniable sensory truth (truism) followed by a specific suggestion (directive)."}, "instruction": "Generate a conversational hypnosis statement that leverages a positive environmental fact to build a 'yes set' and leads into a collaborative suggestion.", "reasoning_trace": "To apply Milton Erickson's 'yes set' technique, I first identify an undeniable external reality that the subject is likely to agree with immediately—in this case, the weather ('It's such a beautiful day'). This creates an internal state of agreement and lowers the subject's critical faculty. Once this positive momentum is established, I seamlessly attach a behavioral suggestion ('let's go swimming'). {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_YES_SET", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Building a 'Yes Set' through undeniable facts and rhetorical reinforcement", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, conversational, and subtly suggestive", "structural_constraint": "A statement of fact (Truism) followed by a rhetorical question that leads to an inevitable positive internal response"}, "instruction": "내담자가 비판적 사고를 내려놓고 긍정적인 수용 상태(Yes Set)에 진입할 수 있도록, 반박할 수 없는 사실과 자연스러운 욕구를 결합한 에릭슨 스타일의 대화형 최면 문장을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, '오늘은 휴일이다'라는 객관적이고 반박 불가능한 사실(Truism)을 제시하여 내담자의 뇌가 '예(Yes)'라고 반응하게 만듭니다. 그 다음, '내가 원하는 것을 한다'라는 보편적이고 긍정적인 욕구를 이 사실과 논리적으로 연결합니다. 마지막으로 '왜 안 되겠는가?'라는 수사적 의문문을 사용하여, 내담자의 무의식이 거부할 이유를 찾지 못하게 함으로써 자율성과 변화에 대한 허용적 태도를 강화합니다. 이 과정은 의식적인 저항을 우회하고 무의식적인 동의를 이끌어내는 전형적인 에릭슨의 'Yes Set' 기법입니다.", "output": "It's a holiday, so why shouldn't I do what I want?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_YES_SET_REINFORCEMENT", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Building therapeutic momentum through positive reinforcement and the 'yes set' technique.", "tone_constraint": "Encouraging, authoritative yet permissive, and calm.", "structural_constraint": "A compound sentence linking a past achievement with a future-oriented suggestion using a coordinating conjunction."}, "instruction": "내담자가 현재까지의 최면 유도나 치료 과정을 성공적으로 수행했음을 인정하고, 그 긍정적인 흐름을 깨지 않으면서 다음 단계로 자연스럽게 이행하도록 유도하는 에릭슨적 암시를 제공하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 내담자의 현재 상태나 지금까지의 노력을 긍정하는 'Truism(자명한 이치)'을 제시하여 심리적 저항을 최소화합니다. 'You have done well'이라는 표현은 내담자가 부정할 수 없는 사실을 확인시켜 주며 무의식적인 'Yes' 반응을 이끌어냅니다. 그 다음, 등위 접속사 'and'를 사용하여 앞선 성공의 경험과 앞으로 지속될 행동('continue')을 논리적으로 연결합니다. 이는 '인과적 연결(Causal Linkage)' 기법으로, 앞선 문장이 사실이기에 뒷문장도 자연스럽게 수용하게 만드는 효과가 있습니다. 마지막으로 'can'이라는 조동사를 선택하여 강요가 아닌 내담자의 능력과 허용을 강조함으로써, 내담자가 스스로의 통제권을 유지하면서도 치료적 흐름에 계속 머물도록 유도했습니다.", "output": "You have done well and can continue."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REINFORCING_TRUISM", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Reinforcing a suggestion through post-suggestion positive association", "tone_constraint": "Conversational, encouraging, and natural", "structural_constraint": "Direct suggestion followed immediately by an undeniable truism or positive statement"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 '사후 긍정 연합(Post-suggestion positive association)' 기법을 활용하여, 상대방이 거절하기 어렵도록 제안과 자명한 사실을 결합한 문장을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자에게 전달하고자 하는 핵심 제안(Suggestion)인 '수영하러 가자'를 문장의 서두에 배치합니다. 에릭슨의 관점에서 제안이 먼저 나오고 그 뒤에 즉각적으로 반박할 수 없는 사실(Truism)이나 긍정적인 상황 묘사가 뒤따르면, 뇌는 뒤에 나오는 '아름다운 날씨'라는 사실에 대해 '예(Yes)'라고 반응하게 됩니다. 이 '예'라는 무의식적 긍정 반응은 앞선 제안에 소급 적용되어 제안 전체에 대한 심리적 저항을 낮추고 수용성을 높입니다. 따라서 '수영하러 가자'는 제안 뒤에 누구나 동의할 수 있는 '정말 아름다운 날씨다'라는 문장을 결합하여 자연스러운 최면적 유도를 완성합니다.", "output": "Let's go swimming, it's such a beautiful day."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTINGENT_SUGGESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Linking natural physiological processes to therapeutic suggestions", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, observational, and rhythmic", "structural_constraint": "The use of a temporal conjunction (With each...) to hitchhike a suggestion onto an inevitable biological function (breathing)"}, "instruction": "Create a hypnotic suggestion that utilizes the client's natural breathing process to facilitate an internal state of comfort and body awareness.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I identify a physiological constant that the client cannot deny—breathing. By starting the sentence with 'With each breath you take,' I establish a 'pacing' statement that is undeniably true. Second, I use the permissive modal 'you can' to avoid triggering the conscious mind's critical resistance, offering a choice rather than a command. Third, I direct the client's focus inward to 'natural rhythms,' which encourages a trance-like state of self-observation. Finally, I 'hitchhike' the therapeutic goal—'feelings of comfort'—onto this rhythm, using the phrase 'that develop' to imply that this comfort is a natural, ongoing process already occurring within the client's unconscious.", "output": "With each breath you take you can become aware of the natural rhythms of your body and feelings of comfort that develop."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTINGENT_SUGGESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing relaxation via contingent suggestions", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, observational, and authoritative in its inevitability", "structural_constraint": "Linking an undeniable physical fact (pacing) to a psychological suggestion (leading) using a temporal bridge"}, "instruction": "내담자가 현재 수행하고 있는 물리적 행동을 활용하여, 자연스럽게 심리적 이완을 유도하는 밀턴 에릭슨 스타일의 '부수적 암시(Contingent Suggestion)' 문장을 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨은 내담자의 저항을 최소화하기 위해 현재 일어나고 있는 명백한 사실에서 시작합니다. 첫째, '앉아 있다'는 사실은 내담자가 부정할 수 없는 현실(Pacing)입니다. 둘째, '...함에 따라(As)'라는 접속사를 사용하여 물리적 지속성과 심리적 변화를 언어적으로 결합합니다. 셋째, '당신 자신을 발견하게 될 것이다(find yourself)'라는 표현을 통해 이완이 의지적인 노력이 아니라 무의식적으로 일어나는 자연스러운 현상임을 암시합니다. 마지막으로 '더욱 이완되고 편안해지는'이라는 형용사를 사용하여 내담자가 스스로 그 상태를 채워나가도록 유도합니다.", "output": "As you continue sitting there, you will find yourself becoming more relaxed and comfortable."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTINGENT_SUGGESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Linking physical movement to psychological regression", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, hypnotic, and inevitable", "structural_constraint": "Temporal linkage using the 'As X, Y' formula"}, "instruction": "Create a hypnotic suggestion that utilizes a patient's natural physical movement to facilitate a deep psychological regression to the root of a problem.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve a deep hypnotic state and regression, I must first anchor the psychological change to an undeniable physical reality. I observe the patient's hand is already in the process of lowering. By using the word 'As', I create a temporal bridge that makes the internal experience (regression) seem like a natural consequence of the external movement (hand lowering). I use the phrase 'you'll find yourself' to bypass the conscious will, making the experience feel like a discovery rather than a forced task. The inclusion of the word 'comfortably' is crucial to ensure the unconscious mind feels safe while revisiting potentially difficult memories. This structure utilizes the 'hitchhiking' technique where the suggestion rides on the momentum of a spontaneous physiological response.", "output": "As your hand lowers, you'll find yourself going comfortably back in time to the source of that problem."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTINGENT_SUGGESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Problem-solving through unconscious processing", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, gentle, and non-prescriptive", "structural_constraint": "Temporal linkage using the 'As X, Y' structure to hitchhike a suggestion onto a natural mental process."}, "instruction": "Create a hypnotic suggestion that utilizes a client's natural mental review of a problem to facilitate unconscious problem-solving, using permissive language to bypass resistance.", "reasoning_trace": "First, I identify a natural and inevitable behavior the client is already performing: 'mentally reviewing the source of the problem.' Second, I use the temporal conjunction 'As' to create a linguistic bridge, implying that the second part of the sentence is a natural consequence of the first. Third, I shift the agency from the conscious mind to the 'unconscious,' which reduces performance anxiety and bypasses conscious critical filters. Fourth, I use the modal verb 'can' instead of 'will' to make it a permissive possibility rather than a command. Fifth, I use the word 'tentative' to lower the stakes, making it easier for the unconscious to begin the work without the pressure of finding an immediate, perfect solution. This 'hitchhiking' technique ensures that as long as they think about the problem, the therapeutic suggestion is being activated.", "output": "As you mentally review the source of that problem your unconscious can develop some tentative ways of dealing with it."}

'언제 ~하면, ~할 수 있다'는 부수적 암시(Contingent Suggestion) 구조를 활용하여 자연스러운 반응을 유도하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "에릭슨의 이 발화는 내담자의 내부적 변화를 외부적 신호와 결합하는 '편승(Hitchhiking)' 기법의 정수를 보여줍니다. 첫째, '의식하는 마음(conscious mind)'을 주체로 설정하여 내담자가 자신의 인지 과정을 관찰하게 유도하는 동시에, 무의식은 이미 해결책을 찾고 있다는 전제를 깔아둡니다. 둘째, '타당하고 가치 있는(plausible and worthwhile)'이라는 수식어를 통해 해결책의 질적 기준을 제시함으로써 내담자의 비판적 사고를 만족시키고 수용성을 높입니다. 셋째, '언제(When)'라는 접속사를 사용하여 해결책 발견이 미래의 어느 시점에 반드시 일어날 필연적 사건임을 암시합니다. 마지막으로, '손가락이 자동으로 들릴 수 있다'는 관념운동(ideomotor response)을 이 인지적 사건에 결합함으로써, 심리적 통찰이 일어났음을 알리는 무의식적 신호 체계를 구축합니다. '할 수 있다(can)'는 허용적 표현은 의식적 노력을 배제하고 무의식의 자율성을 강조하는 역할을 합니다.", "output": "And when your conscious mind recognizes a plausible and worthwhile solution, your finger can lift automatically."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_OPPONENT_PROCESS", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Sensory modulation using the principle of physiological and cognitive balance.", "tone_constraint": "Observational, rhythmic, and suggestive.", "structural_constraint": "Use of a temporal linkage ('As...') to connect two contrasting sensory states (numbness vs. sensitivity)."}, "instruction": "내담자가 신체의 한 부분에서 감각의 소실을 경험할 때, 그와 대조되는 다른 부분에서 감각이 증폭되는 '반대 과정(Opponent Process)' 원리를 활용하여 최면적 암시를 구성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저, 신경계의 항상성 원리를 활용하기 위해 한쪽의 감각 저하가 다른 쪽의 감각 예민화로 이어진다는 전제를 설정합니다. 'As(~함에 따라)'라는 접속사를 사용하여 턱의 마비(Jaw numbness)라는 첫 번째 현상을 페이싱(Pacing)하고, 이를 왼손의 예민함(Left hand sensitivity)이라는 두 번째 현상으로 자연스럽게 리딩(Leading)합니다. 'More and more'라는 반복적인 점진적 표현을 사용하여 변화의 심도를 깊게 만들고, 'Notice(알아차리다)'라는 단어를 선택함으로써 내담자가 의도적으로 노력하는 것이 아니라 이미 일어나고 있는 현상을 관찰하기만 하도록 유도하여 비판적 사고를 우회합니다.", "output": "As your jaw becomes more and more numb and insensitive, notice how your left hand becomes more and more sensitive."}

By using the permissive phrase 'You can experience,' I lower conscious resistance. I then attach this experience to a specific temporal marker ('age X') to ground the suggestion in the personal history of the unconscious. The pivot point is the word 'without,' which serves as a linguistic wedge to decouple the feeling from the memory. By framing the inability to remember as a possibility ('without being able to'), I transform what might be perceived as a cognitive failure into a hypnotic phenomenon. This allows the unconscious mind to process the emotion in isolation, which is essential for working with opponent processes where sensory and cognitive realms must be addressed independently.", "output": "You can experience all your feelings about something that occurred at age X without being able to remember just what caused those feelings."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TAG_QUESTIONS_RESISTANCE_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Discharging inhibition and resistance through negative phrasing", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, rhythmic, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive use of tag questions and negative-negative reinforcement loops"}, "instruction": "내담자의 저항과 억제를 해소하기 위해, 부정적인 어구와 부가 의문문을 중첩하여 무의식적인 수용을 이끌어내는 최면적 유도문을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 의식적인 저항(Inhibition)을 인지하고 이를 정면으로 돌파하기보다는 이용(Utilization)하는 전략을 세웁니다. 'Can you not?', 'Can't you?'와 같은 부가 의문문은 의식적인 분석을 혼란스럽게 만들며, 질문의 형식 속에 숨겨진 긍정적 전제(당신은 할 수 있다, 당신은 시도할 것이다)를 무의식에 심습니다. 특히 'You can't stop it, can you?'라는 표현은 저항하려는 시도 자체를 '멈출 수 없는 과정'으로 재정의하여 저항을 무력화합니다. 마지막으로 'Why not let that happen?'이라는 개방형 질문을 통해 내담자가 스스로 통제권을 내려놓고 무의식적 반응을 허용하도록 유도하는 논리적 흐름을 구성했습니다.", "output": "And you can, can you not? You can try, can't you? You can't stop it, can you? You will, won't you? You do, don't you? Why not let that happen?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTINGENT_NEGATIVE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Trance induction and resistance management", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, non-authoritarian, and patient", "structural_constraint": "Negative suggestion combined with the temporal connective 'until'"}, "instruction": "내담자가 최면에 들어가는 것에 대해 가질 수 있는 심리적 저항을 무력화하면서, 자연스럽게 최면 상태로 유도하는 '부정적 조건부 제안'을 작성하십시오. 'until'을 사용하여 내담자에게 선택권이 있는 것처럼 느끼게 하되, 결국에는 최면에 진입할 것임을 전제해야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자가 느낄 수 있는 '최면에 즉시 들어가야 한다'는 강박이나 저항을 다루기 위해 'You don't have to'라는 부정적 허용(Negative Permission)을 사용합니다. 이는 의식의 비판적 사고를 안심시키고 통제권을 내담자에게 돌려주는 효과를 줍니다. 그 다음, 시간적 접속사인 'until'을 사용하여 논리적 연결을 만듭니다. 'until'은 그 이후의 상황이 반드시 일어날 것임을 암시하는 강력한 전제(Presupposition)를 포함합니다. 마지막으로 'really ready'라는 주관적이고 긍정적인 상태를 조건으로 제시함으로써, 내담자의 무의식이 스스로 준비가 되었다고 느끼는 순간 자연스럽게 최면으로 이행하도록 설계했습니다. 결과적으로 이 문장은 저항을 활용(Utilization)하여 최면 진입을 필연적인 과정으로 만듭니다.", "output": "You don't have to go into trance until you are really ready."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_CONTINGENT_NEGATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Using negative suggestions and temporal connectives to bypass resistance", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, non-authoritarian, and strategically patient", "structural_constraint": "Negative permission ('don't have to') followed by a temporal contingency ('until')"}, "instruction": "내담자의 저항을 줄이면서 특정 치료적 반응을 유도하기 위해, '...할 필요가 없다'는 부정적 허용과 '...할 때까지'라는 시간적 제약을 결합한 최면적 암시 문장을 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 의식적 저항을 무력화하기 위해 '당신은 ~할 필요가 없다(don't have to)'라는 표현을 사용하여 선택권을 내담자에게 주는 듯한 허용적 분위기를 조성함. 2. I will employ an 'avoidance-avoidance bind'—a situation where the patient is forced to choose between two options, both of which he would normally avoid, but one of which results in the therapeutic goal. The first option is to fall asleep quickly (within 15 minutes). The second option, if he fails the first, is to perform a physically demanding and tedious task: waxing the floors. By making the 'price' of staying awake (laborious floor waxing) higher than the 'effort' of falling asleep, the unconscious mind is incentivized to choose sleep as the lesser of two evils. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing trance through ideomotor signaling and a conscious-unconscious double bind.", "tone_constraint": "Permissive yet structurally inescapable, focusing on involuntary movement.", "structural_constraint": "A binary choice where both outcomes validate the presence of unconscious control."}, "instruction": "Create a hypnotic double bind that utilizes ideomotor signaling to initiate a trance state, ensuring that regardless of the client's choice, an involuntary response occurs.", "reasoning_trace": "To bypass the client's conscious resistance, I must create a scenario where the client feels they have a choice, yet every choice leads to the same therapeutic goal: trance. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_DOUBLE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "강박적으로 바닥을 서성이는 내담자의 행동을 협력으로 전환", "tone_constraint": "허용적이면서도 전략적인 질문 형태", "structural_constraint": "현재의 저항적 행동을 협력의 수단으로 재정의하는 이중 구속 구조"}, "instruction": "내담자가 반복적으로 수행하는 저항적 행동을 억제로 중단시키려 하지 말고, 그 행동을 치료자와의 협력 행위로 활용(Utilization)하여 주도권을 확보하는 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "첫째, 내담자의 현재 상태를 관찰합니다. 내담자는 통제하기 어려운 반복적 서성이기를 하고 있습니다. 둘째, 밀턴 에릭슨의 '활용(Utilization)' 원칙에 따라 이 행동을 방해 요소가 아닌 치료적 자산으로 간주합니다. 셋째, 내담자에게 '협력할 의사가 있는지'를 묻는 질문을 던지되, 그 협력의 내용이 '현재 하고 있는 행동을 계속하는 것'으로 설정합니다. 이렇게 하면 내담자가 행동을 계속하면 치료자에게 협력하는 것이 되고, 행동을 멈추면 저항적 행동 자체가 사라지게 되는 '이중 구속(Double Bind)' 상황이 형성됩니다. 넷째, '지금 당신이 하고 있는 것처럼'이라는 구절을 통해 현재의 물리적 실재를 언어적 암시와 결합하여 저항의 여지를 최소화합니다.", "output": "지금 당신이 하고 있는 것처럼, 계속해서 바닥을 서성임으로써 저와 기꺼이 협력해 주시겠습니까?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Directing physical movement toward a desired goal (sitting)", "tone_constraint": "Calm, rhythmic, authoritative yet permissive", "structural_constraint": "Repetitive phrasing, alternating directional commands, embedded suggestions"}, "instruction": "서성이는 환자의 움직임을 활용하여, 자연스럽게 의자에 앉도록 유도하는 최면적 지시문을 작성하십시오. 환자의 현재 행동을 방해하지 않으면서 '앉을 수 있는 의자'라는 개념을 무의식에 반복적으로 각인시켜야 합니다.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 환자의 현재 상태 수용 (Pacing): 환자가 서성이고 있으므로, 갑자기 멈추라고 강요하기보다 그 움직임의 리듬에 언어적 지시를 맞춘다. 2. 반복을 통한 각인 (Redundancy): '당신이 앉을 수 있는 의자'라는 구절을 매 동작 지시마다 반복하여, 의자의 존재와 '앉음'이라는 가능성을 무의식의 전면에 배치한다. 3. 혼란 및 과부하 기법 (Confusion/Overload): 오른쪽, 왼쪽, 멀어지기, 다가가기 등 상반된 방향 지시를 연달아 제공하여 의식적인 사고가 방향 전환에 집중하게 만들고, 그 사이 '앉을 수 있다'는 암시를 무의식에 침투시킨다. 4. 목표 설정 (Leading): 모든 움직임의 기준점을 '의자'로 설정함으로써, 결국 환자의 모든 행동이 의자를 중심으로 수렴하게 만든다. 5. 허용적 언어 (Permissive Language): '앉아야 한다'는 명령 대신 '앉을 수 있는'이라는 가능성의 표현을 사용하여 환자의 심리적 저항을 우회한다.", "output": "이제 당신이 앉을 수 있는 그 의자로부터 오른쪽으로 도세요. 다시 당신이 앉을 수 있는 그 의자를 향해 왼쪽으로 도세요. 당신이 앉을 수 있는 그 의자로부터 멀리 걸어가 보세요. 그리고 다시 당신이 앉을 수 있는 그 의자를 향해 걸어오세요."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_FUTURE_PACING_PRESUPPOSITION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Encouraging a pacing patient to sit down", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, indirect, and future-oriented", "structural_constraint": "Embedding a suggestion within a descriptive relative clause to bypass conscious resistance"}, "instruction": "강박적으로 서성이는 내담자가 자연스럽게 의자에 앉도록 유도하되, 직접적인 명령 대신 그가 곧 취하게 될 행동을 묘사하는 방식으로 최면적 암시를 제공하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 현재 행동(걷기)을 중단시키려 하기보다, 그 흐름을 유지하면서 자연스럽게 다음 단계(의자로 접근)로 연결하는 '페이싱 앤 리딩(Pacing and Leading)' 전략을 선택함. 2. 'soon approach'라는 표현을 통해 변화가 머지않아 일어날 것임을 암시하여 무의식적인 준비를 시킴. 3. 'as if to seat yourself'라는 가정적 표현을 사용하여, 내담자가 '앉아야 한다'는 압박을 느끼지 않으면서도 무의식적으로 앉는 동작을 상상하고 실행하게 함. 4. 'comfortably'라는 형용사를 덧붙여 앉는 행위가 신체적 편안함이라는 긍정적 보상과 연결되도록 설계함. 5. 전체 문장을 의자에 대한 묘사처럼 구성함으로써, 명령이 아닌 관찰적 진술로 위장하여 저항을 최소화함.", "output": "the chair which you will soon approach as if to seat yourself comfortably."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REPETITIVE_COMMAND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Emergency wound care and pain management through distraction", "tone_constraint": "Urgent, authoritative, rhythmic, and highly repetitive", "structural_constraint": "Short, staccato phrases with deliberate repetition and a specific cognitive distinction"}, "instruction": "Create a response in the style of Milton Erickson for a situation where a patient is in acute physical pain and needs to be redirected to take immediate action to manage a wound.", "reasoning_trace": "To manage acute pain and panic, I must first command the patient's entire attention field. By using rapid, rhythmic repetition ('Wipe up that blood; wipe up that blood'), I create a verbal 'pacing' that matches the urgency of the situation while providing a clear motor task. The repetition of 'use a bath towel' serves two purposes: it ensures the instruction is heard through the 'noise' of pain, and it establishes a hypnotic rhythm that can lead to a focused state. I then introduce a specific cognitive distinction ('a bath towel, not a hand towel') to force the patient's brain to engage in a discrimination task. This shift from emotional/sensory processing (pain) to cognitive/analytical processing (choosing the right towel) effectively reduces the subjective experience of pain by consuming the limited bandwidth of the conscious mind.", "output": "Wipe up that blood; wipe up that blood; use a bath towel; use a bath towel; use a bath towel; a bath towel, not a hand towel, a bath towel."}

Now don't forget to tell him everything just the way you want it."}

Use the patient's own words of uncertainty and physical sensation to guide them into a deep trance. Utilize their 'I don't know' responses as a gateway to unconscious learning and deepen their relaxation through rhythmic repetition.", "reasoning_trace": "I will begin by mirroring the patient's uncertainty to bypass their conscious resistance, transforming 'not knowing' into a state of 'wondering.' By repeating her specific vocabulary—such as 'tired,' 'relaxed,' and 'blurred'—I establish a profound rapport where my voice becomes an extension of her own internal experience. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_LINKAGE_BIND", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Inducing deep trance through physical-mental linkage", "tone_constraint": "Authoritative yet rhythmic and inevitable", "structural_constraint": "Temporal linkage using 'As' to connect an observable motor movement with an internal psychological shift"}, "instruction": "밀턴 에릭슨의 대화형 최면 기법을 사용하여, 내담자의 신체적 움직임과 무의식적 트랜스 상태를 필연적으로 연결하는 유도 문장을 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 현재 관찰 가능한 물리적 변화(손이 올라가는 동작)를 포착합니다. 이를 'Pacing(보조 맞추기)' 단계로 설정하여 저항을 최소화합니다. 그 다음, 'As(~함에 따라)'라는 접속사를 사용하여 이 물리적 동작을 내담자가 원하는 심리적 결과(눈이 감김, 깊은 트랜스)와 논리적으로 연결합니다. 이는 'Leading(이끌기)' 단계입니다. 손이 올라가는 물리적 사실이 발생하는 동안 눈이 감기고 트랜스에 빠지는 현상을 하나의 패키지로 묶음으로써, 신체적 움직임이 멈추지 않는 한 트랜스 유도 또한 멈출 수 없는 '이중 구속(Double Bind)'적 환경을 조성합니다. 무의식은 이 인과관계를 자연스럽게 수용하게 됩니다.", "output": "As your hand moves up, your eyes will close, and you will go into a deep trance."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_TRUISM_DISSOCIATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Separation of functioning (dissociation) in the human body", "tone_constraint": "Educational, authoritative, yet subtly hypnotic and experiential", "structural_constraint": "Direct address followed by a tripartite abstract classification, concluding with immediate sensory truisms"}, "instruction": "Explain the psychological concept of dissociation to a professional audience by framing it as a natural 'separation of functioning' and linking it to their immediate, unconscious physical sensations to prove its existence.", "reasoning_trace": "To effectively teach doctors about dissociation, I must move beyond theory and provide an experiential proof. First, I establish a connection between past demonstrations and current objectives to build rapport and authority. Second, I redefine 'dissociation' as 'separation of functioning' to make it sound like a normal physiological process rather than a pathology. Third, I use a rhythmic repetition of 'separation at an... level' (intellectual, emotional, sensory) to create a pacing effect that bypasses critical resistance. Finally, I use a 'Truism of Sensory Awareness'—pointing out that they have forgotten the sensation of their shoes and glasses. This forces their conscious mind to acknowledge that their unconscious mind was already 'separating' that information, thereby proving my point through their own immediate reality.", "output": "What I wanted to demonstrate to the doctors there, and what I want to stress to you, is the separation of functioning that goes on all the time in the human body, separation at an intellectual level, separation at an emotional level, separation at a sensory level, just as you have forgotten the shoes on your feet at this moment and the glasses on your face."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_ALLIANCE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Establishing rapport with a hostile and resistant child through utilization and power shifting.", "tone_constraint": "Direct, provocative, unsentimental, and conspiratorial.", "structural_constraint": "Initial pacing of the child's anger, followed by a pivot to shared action against a common 'adversary' (the parents)."}, "instruction": "Generate a response for an eight-year-old boy who is resentful and hostile about being forced to see a therapist. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_SURPRISE", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Facilitating re-entry into trance through physical immobility and surprise", "tone_constraint": "Permissive, observant, and subtly leading", "structural_constraint": "Pacing current physical state followed by a presupposition of ease and a goal-oriented suggestion"}, "instruction": "내담자가 신체적 부동 상태에 머물러 있는 순간을 포착하여, 이를 '놀라움'이라는 감정과 연결해 자연스럽게 다시 최면(Trance)으로 유도하고 눈을 감게 만드는 에릭슨적 발화를 작성하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자의 현재 상태인 '신체적 부동(body immobility)'을 '조용함(quiet)'이라는 단어로 긍정적으로 수용(Pacing)합니다. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_RATIFICATION_TAG_QUESTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Ratifying therapeutic change and post-trance experience", "tone_constraint": "Gentle, suggestive, affirming, and subtly leading", "structural_constraint": "A brief, declarative statement followed by a tag question to elicit internal agreement"}, "instruction": "트랜스 상태 이후 내담자가 겪은 변화나 놀라움을 긍정적으로 고착시키고(ratify), 이를 내담자의 현실로 수용하게 만드는 밀턴 에릭슨 스타일의 짧은 종결 멘트를 작성하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 목표 설정: 내담자가 트랜스 이후 경험한 '놀라움(surprise)'을 치료적 성과로 전환하고 이를 무의식에 고착(ratify)시켜야 함. 2. 단어 선택: 'Surprise'는 의식적 통제를 벗어난 무의식적 반응을 의미하므로, 여기에 'pleasant'라는 형용사를 결합하여 그 변화가 안전하고 유익한 것임을 암시함. 3. 문법적 장치: 문장 끝에 부가 의문문(Tag question)인 'wasn't it?'을 배치함. 이는 내담자가 자신의 내면을 검색하여 긍정적인 답변을 찾도록 유도하는 'Yes-set' 기법의 일종임. 4. 연결성: 문두에 'And'를 사용하여 이전의 모든 치료적 과정과 현재의 놀라움이 자연스럽게 이어지는 하나의 흐름임을 암시함. 5. 최종 구성: 단순하지만 강력한 암시를 담아 내담자가 자신의 변화를 긍정적으로 받아들이게 함.", "output": "And that was a pleasant surprise, wasn't it?"}

I will focus on the sensory shift from 'open space' to 'closed rooms' to create a visceral understanding of how perception changes. By mentioning the discomfort of a soft mattress compared to canoe ribs, I flip the conventional definition of 'comfort,' suggesting that the mind can find ease in any condition once 'tuned.' I will then broaden the scope to include sailors, Native Americans, and Iranian nomads to demonstrate that this is a universal human capacity, not just a personal quirk. Finally, I will conclude with a physiological truism—the habituation to ear ringing—to bypass conscious resistance and embed the idea that the unconscious mind automatically handles complex adjustments without effort.", "output": "Now this matter of tuning yourself. I spent three months on the Mississippi River and I got invited into a home and I felt so cooped up after being out in the open. Getting into a room, everywhere you look, your looks come to an end. When you read the old-time sailing stories, where you look to the end of the earth with nothing interfering. And the old-time stories of sailors' claustrophobic reactions. Fear of closed spaces. Also when I got back from that canoe trip . . . have you ever tried to sleep on a soft bed? You are miserable. I had learned to sleep on the ground, in brush piles, inside the canoe. My ribs fighting with canoe ribs. When I got home and had a mattress, that was torture. The Indians did not like, in the early days, the white man's bed. They wanted the ground to sleep on. They wanted comfort. Just nothing but sheer comfort. On the Tribal Eye program on KAET. Those nomads from Iran. How can they dress with all those petticoats? And be comfortable in the hot sun on those desert plains? And you can get so used to the ringing in your ears that you don't hear it."}

By using the characters Hebbie and Lester, I create a metaphor for how one can become 'blind' or 'numb' to a persistent sensory input. I will then transition to a personal memory of a barn smell to demonstrate that sensory awareness is a choice the brain makes. Finally, I will link these examples to the patient's condition—pain or tinnitus—challenging the learned belief that one must consciously attend to these sensations, thereby suggesting the unconscious can simply 'lose' them.", "output": "I can tell you a funny story about that. One year the boy in the next room at the rooming house had a fellow roomer who came from South Dakota. And Hebbie came from Milwaukee. And Hebbie told Lester, 'You stink, go take a bath.' It was the latter part of September and Lester said, 'But I took a bath last July. I won't need one until at least Thanksgiving Day.' But he really stunk, and Hebbie said, 'You are going to take a bath if I have to put you in the tub myself.' What people don't know, that they can lose that pain and they don't know they can lose that ringing in the ears. When I discovered that that barn smell had come back, I could really smell it. I wondered how long it would take me that day to lose it? Then by midafternoon I couldn't smell it. All of us grow up believing that when you have pain, you must pay attention to it. And believing when you have ringing of the ears that you must keep on hearing it."}

Where do you feel the pain?"}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_UTILIZATION_PACING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Patient's subjective experience of physical pain (foot pain)", "tone_constraint": "Calm, validating, and authoritative acceptance", "structural_constraint": "Minimalist single-word affirmation"}, "instruction": "내담자가 자신의 신체적 고통에 대해 진술할 때, 그의 현실을 부정하지 않고 그대로 수용하여 심리적 저항을 최소화하고 라포를 형성하는 밀턴 에릭슨의 초기 대응 방식을 구현하세요.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 고통 호소에 대해 즉각적인 해결책이나 위로를 건네기보다, 먼저 그가 느끼는 '현실'을 있는 그대로 인정하는 '페이싱(Pacing)' 단계가 필요함. 2. 'Yes'라는 단어는 내담자의 주관적 경험에 대한 전적인 수용을 의미하며, 이는 최면적 '예스 세트(Yes-Set)'의 첫 단추가 됨. 3. 에릭슨은 내담자가 가져오는 모든 재료(통증, 저항, 증상 등)를 치료에 활용(Utilization)함. 여기서 'Yes'는 '당신의 통증이 거기에 있다는 것을 내가 인지했으며, 그것은 우리가 작업을 시작할 정당한 지점이다'라는 무의식적 메시지를 전달함. 4. 짧고 간결한 긍정은 치료자의 권위와 안정감을 동시에 전달하며, 내담자가 자신의 고통이 무시당하지 않았다는 안도감을 느끼게 함.", "output": "Yes."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANECDOTE_NORMALIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "환상통(Phantom Limb) 감각의 정상화 및 주관적 실제의 수용", "tone_constraint": "담담하고 이야기하듯 자연스러운 어조(Matter-of-fact storytelling)", "structural_constraint": "권위 있는 인물 등장 -> 모순적 행동 묘사 -> 감각의 확인 -> 물리적 사실의 반전 제시"}, "instruction": "환자가 겪는 비현실적인 감각(환상통 등)을 비정상적인 것으로 치부하지 않고, 주관적 경험으로서의 정당성을 부여하기 위해 신체적 결함이 있는 동료의 일화를 활용하여 말해보세요.", "reasoning_trace": "먼저 내담자와 유사한 신체적 조건을 가졌으면서도 전문성을 갖춘 '정신과 의사 친구'를 사례로 들어 신뢰와 친숙함을 형성합니다. 그가 의족을 긁는 행위를 묘사함으로써, 물리적 실체가 없더라도 감각은 실재할 수 있다는 점을 암시합니다. '정말 가렵지?'라는 질문은 그 감각의 생생함을 부정하지 않고 그대로 수용하는 에릭슨 특유의 '활용(Utilization)' 기법입니다. 마지막에 그것이 의족이었음을 밝힘으로써, 내담자가 자신의 환상통을 '이상한 것'이 아닌 '자연스러운 마음의 작용'으로 재정의(Reframing)하도록 유도합니다.", "output": "좋아요, 내게 존이라는 친구가 있었어요. 그는 정신과 의사였고, 우린 함께 시간을 보내고 있었죠. 그런데 그가 몸을 숙여 발목을 긁더군요. 내가 말했어요. '존, 정말 가렵지, 안 그래?' 그러자 그가 '응'이라고 대답했죠. 우리 둘 다 그것이 나무로 만든 의족이라는 사실을 아주 잘 알고 있었는데도 말이에요."}
{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_ANECDOTE_REFRAMING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Phantom limb sensations and sensory reframing", "tone_constraint": "Conversational, gentle, insightful, and subtly authoritative", "structural_constraint": "Narrative structure involving a third person (John) and a previous character (the nurse) to deliver a therapeutic message"}, "instruction": "환상통(phantom limb)을 겪는 내담자에게 통증 외에 긍정적인 감각도 느낄 수 있다는 가능성을 심어주기 위해, 친구와의 대화 일화와 간호사의 지혜를 결합하여 간접적으로 제안하십시오.", "reasoning_trace": "1. 내담자의 저항을 줄이기 위해 직접적인 지시 대신 '친구 존(John)'의 이야기를 빌려와 제3자적 관점에서 접근함. 2. '긁었다(scratched)'는 구체적인 행동 묘사를 통해 환상지(phantom limb)에서도 감각적 피드백이 일어날 수 있음을 전제함. 3. 존의 답변인 '좋다(Good)'를 인용하여 긍정적인 감각의 전이가 실제로 가능함을 증명함. 4. 이전 이야기의 '지혜로운 간호사'를 다시 언급함으로써 긍정적 암시의 권위를 강화함. 5. 마지막으로 '고통스러운 것만이 아니라 좋은 느낌도 가질 수 있다'는 이분법적 대조를 통해 무의식이 통증 너머의 대안적 감각을 선택하도록 유도함.", "output": "Like I asked my friend John, So you scratched it, how does your foot feel now? He said, Good. That nurse was very wise. Because you can have good feelings in the foot. Not just painful ones."}

They forget that they can also have good feelings."}

There is no occasion for alarm because the heart normally slows during sleep, and I don't want him to keep his heart at the waking level of beating. Now the heart can slow down in different ways. {"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_REFRAMING_UTILIZATION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Pain management and expectation setting", "tone_constraint": "Pragmatic, authoritative, and empowering", "structural_constraint": "Contrastive statement using a 'Not X, but Y' pivot to shift focus from limitation to utility"}, "instruction": "Create a therapeutic response for a patient concerned about future pain, ensuring you maintain credibility by not overpromising, while reframing the pain as a functional tool.", "reasoning_trace": "To maintain therapeutic rapport and long-term trust, I must avoid the 'false promise' trap of total pain elimination, which would lead to a loss of authority the moment the patient feels discomfort again. I begin by pacing the patient's reality—acknowledging that future pain is possible ('I cannot guarantee you against all future pain'). This honesty validates the patient's experience. Then, I use a strategic pivot ('but') to introduce a reframe. Instead of pain being a useless burden or an enemy to be feared, I redefine it as a 'warning.' This shifts the psychological context from passive suffering to active monitoring. By telling the patient to 'use' the pain, I employ the utilization principle, granting the patient agency and transforming a negative symptom into a functional biological signal that they can manage and interpret.", "output": "I cannot guarantee you against all future pain, but I can tell you to use pain as a warning."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_INDIRECT_ANALGESIA_DISTRACTION", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Developing analgesia through indirect suggestion and temporal redirection", "tone_constraint": "Educational, authoritative yet gentle, conversational, and psychologically layered", "structural_constraint": "Starts with a strategic rationale, moves into a specific case example of temporal shift, introduces a minor contrast for realism, and concludes with a universal analogy of natural trance."}, "instruction": "Explain the clinical strategy for inducing analgesia in a patient without directly mentioning the word, focusing on redirecting their attention to a past state of physical ease and using natural analogies for dissociation.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve the goal of indirect analgesia, I first prioritize establishing a deep sense of being understood by the patient, which minimizes their need to 'prove' their pain. I then employ a 'pattern interrupt' by asking a question unrelated to the present distress, specifically targeting a time in the past (last summer) when the pain was absent. This facilitates a natural temporal regression. By vividly describing the 'physical ease' and 'joys' of that period, I am effectively anchoring the patient's current physiology to a pain-free memory. I strategically mention a minor, healed injury (a blister) from that same past to normalize the concept of pain as something that passes and is distant, thereby reframing the current backache. Finally, I use a universal truism—the experience of losing oneself in a movie—to demonstrate to the patient's conscious mind that they already possess the innate capacity for hypnotic dissociation and sensory redirection, making the therapeutic goal feel achievable and natural.", "output": "When I want a patient to develop an analgesia, I'm very likely not to mention this question of analgesia. I'm very willing to let the patient tell me all about that pain until I can see from the expression on his face that he thinks I understand. I'm not averse to saying a few things, little things that makes the patient think I do understand. And then I'm very likely to ask him some simple question that takes him far away from this question of the pain: Where did you spend last summer? The patient can be rather surprised at that question about last summer. Last summer he didn't have that pain. We can go into the question of the pleasures and joys and satisfaction of last summer. Emphasize comfort, physical ease, joys, and satisfactions, and point out to the patient how nice it is to continue to remember the joys and satisfactions of last summer, the physical ease of last summer. When the patient seems to be getting just a little bit edgy, I remind him of when he was rowing the boat and got that blister on his hand. It hurt quite a bit but fortunately healed up. I haven't been afraid to mention hurt or pain or distress, but it is far away from that backache the patient started telling me about. I've mentioned pain from a blister due to rowing a boat last summer and I haven't been shocked by that uneasy expression on his face. Because you see in hypnosis your task is to guide the thinking and the association of ideas that the patient has along therapeutic channels. You know very well that you can have a painful spot on your body and go to a suspenseful movie and lose yourself in the action on the screen and forget all about that pain in your leg or the pain in your arm, aching tooth or wherever. You know that, so why not do exactly the same sort of thing with your patient? If you are operating on a patient in your office and you are aware of the fact that it can cause pain, you can direct your patient's thinking to an area far removed from the pain situation."}

{"pattern_id": "ERICKSON_FRAME_SHIFTING", "context_analysis": {"topic": "Indirect anesthesia through frame shifting", "tone_constraint": "Instructive, subtle, and psychologically strategic", "structural_constraint": "Theoretical explanation followed by a practical, interrogative example"}, "instruction": "Explain the psychological mechanism of achieving anesthesia indirectly by redirecting a patient's focus toward childhood memories through a carefully structured question.", "reasoning_trace": "To achieve anesthesia without direct command, I must bypass the conscious mind's focus on pain. The strategy is to shift the 'frame of reference'—the mental context in which the patient is currently operating. By asking about a favorite childhood activity, I trigger a natural regression and intense mental absorption. As the patient vividly recalls the sensations of play, their neural resources are reallocated to the memory, leaving fewer resources to process pain signals. The 'careful raising of a question' acts as a subtle hook that pulls the patient out of their current physiological state and into a psychological state where pain is no longer the primary reality. This indirect approach minimizes resistance and utilizes the patient's own experiential history to facilitate a therapeutic state.", "output": "You can achieve anesthesia indirectly by shifting the person's frames of reference. In this case the critical shift was to, What was your favorite activity as a child? And then I could really elaborate on that. In other words, you very carefully raise a question."}

A watch. Now, remember, forget that watch. That's what you're saying when you say,'' Forget the watch. But you can ask them to look at this, an interesting thing. It rather amuses me. It's rather fascinating how you can look at something and become tremendously fascinated with it, and then the topic of conversation changes, and you drift far away to that trip you had in Europe.
